The book-fiend war goes merrily on all
over Australia. The proprietors of one or two
publications have been routed with great
slaughter, and thus lost their chances oi making
thousands of pounds, but so far the Pictokesque
Atlas Company of Ai stpai.asia has been uni-
formly successfully in all courts. 'It is estimated
that up to the present time no less than £14,000
law-costs has been spent by defendants in vain
endeavours to upset the company’s form of con-
tract. It is not generally known that the Atlas,
notwithstanding its huge collections, has not yet
by some scores of thousands of pounds returned
to its proprietors the full amount of their invest-
ment.
A wonderful story of the self-sacrifice and
martyrdom of a nine-year-old boy comes to us
from England. A tale of heroism, mistaken,
perhaps, but nobler and purer than that of all the
conquerors who ever 'sheath 1 .d bloody sword on
victorious battle-field. He was a country lad, one
of a numerous family. Father’s \vages were small,
even dry bread scarcely went round sometimes,
and the little fellow felt that the sixpence a week
he earned bird-scaring did not render him suffi-
ciently self-supporting to excuse his existence. So
one morning ho got up as visual to go to the-fields
and solemnly dividing his few possessions- a
knife, some ha’pence, and broken toys among his
brothers and sisters—kissed them all round and
trudged off to drown himself. But the pond was
shallow, and after repeated failures he walked a
couple of miles further to the railway-line, waited
till the express approached, then knelt down and
laid his little head on the cruel, cold rails, gravely
eyed his executioner as it approached, with
engineers and guards putting on brakes and shout-
ing like maniacs. and then—faded out of life be-
cause his little brothers and sisters were pinched
for bread in the world's wealthiest country;- What
a man the world has lost !
The best card-player Australia ever saw,
and one of the best, perhaps, the world ever saw,
was the Yankee who not many years ago “did”
all tltc “fly ” men this little island could produce.
He cleaned out Maoriland first, but said money
was not over plentiful there. Sydney panned out
better when, amongst other litt'e items, lie
trucked a well-known young grocer, who fancied
himself-at the game, for £500 over a game of poker,
and out Botany way one day lie completely
demoralised the pockets of a 14-stone butcher and
a six-foot-two amateur rowing-man, who thought
they were going to take him down. They accused
him of cheating, and wanted to fight, but he said
a little fellow like him (ho weighed about mile-
stone) would have no show at their style of fight-
ing—however, ho wouldn't mind setting-to
with them in Yankee style. Going out to
the kitchen, he returned with a couple of
carving-knives, and, throwing one down on the
table, said he was not particular who taclded him
first, but they did not see it in the same light, and
there was a big race between them to get out of
the room first. His largest coup, however, was in
Melbourne, when he fleeced a well-known Israelite
to the tune of £4030. When he went to Mel-
bourne a big bazaar was proceeding, and after
attending for a couple of days and going into raffles
and buying button-holes until he became known
to all the stall holders, he invited them to take
tea at his elegant suite of rooms. About 50 ladies
and gentlemen attended his first little reunion,
when champagne flowed like water. Now it hap-
pened that a couple of Hebrews were there who
suggested cards, and the Yank “guessed he
didn’t know much of the game, but he
wasn’t going to spoil fun.” Fairly large stakes
were played for, and the American lost his money-
with the greatest nonchalance ; indeed, in one
hand, when there was quite a pile of money on the
table, he threw down his cards j ust as a young lady
commenced a song, saying : “ I stand out, gentle-
men, and -leave you to it. I am too fond of music
to miss such a beautiful song.” The Hebrews
made quite a good thing that evening, and in a
day ortwo gambling Melbournefairlyrangwith the
fame of the heaven-sent Yankee millionaire all
ready to be shorn. He played his game pluckily,
and lost many hundreds the first night he was
invited out. He could do anything with a pack
of cards, short of making it talk, and he went
through all the Melbourne sharps like small peas
through a large sieve before they “ dropped ” to
his little game. On one cccasion a couple of
downy ones “rung in ” a pack of “readers,” but
they were of no avail, as he usually had half-a-
dozen of the pack on hand after the first deal.
He would run through his cards, exhibiting the
marks so that his opponents would think they
held him safe, and then place them on the table;
but somehow or other he would ring the changes
and beat them, perhaps, by a pip. After winning
a lot of money on this occasion he suddenly put
down his cards and called the waiter to bring him
a pot of paint and a small brush, handing him a
sovereign to purchase them, with. “What
colour ?” asked waiter. “ Oh, it doesn’t matter,”
drawled the Yankee, “ only these gentlemen have
played so long with these cards that they want re-
marking.”
FREETRADE OR PROTECTION.
Some vote Protection, some Freetrade,
As best for this young country’s weal.
But ask the youth or blushing maid,
And each will answer— Pemell’s Meal
As best, because it has been tried.
There’s nothing half so good beside.
His Golden Meal is what I mean,
’Tis good and pure and cheap, I wean.

10th December, 1888.
To H. F. Kugfxmann, Esq.
Dear Sir,—This is to certify that I, Patrick Keenan, was
taken ill about three years ago with a severe cold, which
turned into Bronchitis and became chronic. 1 consulted
more than one doctor, and during that time took a great
quantity of medicine without it doing me the slightest
good, hut I became worse every day, roasting away' until
1 became a perfect skeleton. About February last j began
to spit up blood, and what with the cough and severe
pains in my left lung, and the quantity of bad matter I
was expectorating every day, I became very much alarmed.
Hearing of your professional skill I consulted you, and
yon told me you could cure me for a given sura. I agreed
and went under your treatment in March last. At the
end of three months I was taken bad one morning, and
vomited about two pints of blood, matter and stringy
phlegm. From that time I commenced to improve, and
was gaining in weight every day. About a month ago the
blood ceased coming, the cough disappeared, and the
lung healed completely, and thank God and your pro-
fessional skill, I am as well as ever.
P. KEENAN.
Declared and subscribed before me, one of Her Majesty’s
Justices of the Peace, for the Southern Bailiwick, in the
County of Grant, this 10th day of December, 1888.
Peter Smvtue, J.P.
